In this case it will block for up to {@code max.block.ms} milliseconds if \\n841:      * Kafka cluster is unreachable; 2) Allocating a buffer if buffer pool doesn't have any free buffers.\\n842:      * <p>\\n843:      * The result of the send is a {@link RecordMetadata} specifying the partition the record was sent to, the offset\\n844:      * it was assigned and the timestamp of the record. If the producer is configured with acks = 0, the {@link RecordMetadata}\\n845:      * will have offset = -1 because the producer does not wait for the acknowledgement from the broker.\\n846:      * If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#CREATE_TIME CreateTime} is used by the topic, the timestamp\\n847:      * will be the user provided timestamp or the record send time if the user did not specify a timestamp for the\\n848:      * record. If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME LogAppendTime} is used for the\\n849:      * topic, the timestamp will be the Kafka broker local time when the message is appended.\\n850:      * <p>\\n851:      * Since the send call is asynchronous it returns a {@link java.util.concurrent.Future Future} for the\\n852:      * {@link RecordMetadata} that will be assigned to this record. Invoking {@link java.util.concurrent.Future#get()\\n853:      * get()} on this future will block until the associated request completes and then return the metadata for the record\\n854:      * or throw any exception that occurred while sending the record.\\n855:      * <p>\\n856:      * If you want to simulate a simple blocking call you can call the <code>get()</code> method immediately:\\n857:      *\\n858:      * <pre>\\n859:      * {@code\\n860:      * byte[] key = \\\"key\\\".getBytes();\\n861:      * byte[] value = \\\"value\\\".getBytes();\\n862:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\\\"my-topic\\\", key, value)\\n863:      * producer.send(record).get();\\n864:      * }</pre>\\n865:      * <p>\\n866:      * Fully non-blocking usage can make use of the {@link Callback} parameter to provide a callback that\\n867:      * will be invoked when the request is complete.\\n868:      *\\n869:      * <pre>\\n870:      * {@code\\n871:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\\\"the-topic\\\", key, value);\\n872:      * producer.send(myRecord,\\n873:      *               new Callback() {\\n874:      *                   public void onCompletion(RecordMetadata metadata, Exception e) {\\n875:      *                       if(e != null) {\\n876:      *                          e.printStackTrace();\\n877:      *                       } else {\\n878:      *                          System.out.println(\\\"The offset of the record we just sent is: \\\" + metadata.offset());\\n879:      *                       }\\n880:      *                   }\\n881:      *               });\\n882:      * }\\n883:      * </pre>\\n884:      *\\n885:      * Callbacks for records being sent to the same partition are guaranteed to execute in order. That is, in the\\n886:      * following example <code>callback1</code> is guaranteed to execute before <code>callback2</code>:\\n887:      *\\n888:      * <pre>\\n889:      * {@code\\n890:      * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key1, value1), callback1);\\n891:      * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key2, value2), callback2);\\n892:      * }\\n893:      * </pre>\\n894:      * <p>\\n895:      * When used as part of a transaction, it is not necessary to define a callback or check the result of the future\\n896:      * in order to detect errors from <code>send</code>. If any of the send calls failed with an irrecoverable error,\\n897:      * the final {@link #commitTransaction()} call will fail and throw the exception from the last failed send. When\\n898:      * this happens, your application should call {@link #abortTransaction()} to reset the state and continue to send\\n899:      * data.\\n900:      * </p>\\n901:      * <p>\\n902:      * Some transactional send errors cannot be resolved with a call to {@link #abortTransaction()}.  In particular,\\n903:      * if a transactional send finishes with a {@link ProducerFencedException}, a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.OutOfOrderSequenceException},\\n904:      * a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}, or an\\n905:      * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.AuthorizationException}, then the only option left is to call {@link #close()}.\\n906:      * Fatal errors cause the producer to enter a defunct state in which future API calls will continue to raise\\n907:      * the same underlying error wrapped in a new {@link KafkaException}.\\n908:      * </p>\\n909:      * <p>\\n910:      * It is a similar picture when idempotence is enabled, but no <code>transactional.id</code> has been configured.\\n911:      * In this case, {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException} and\\n912:      * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.AuthorizationException} are considered fatal errors. However,\\n913:      * {@link ProducerFencedException} does not need to be handled. Additionally, it is possible to continue\\n914:      * sending after receiving an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.OutOfOrderSequenceException}, but doing so\\n915:      * can result in out of order delivery of pending messages. To ensure proper ordering, you should close the\\n916:      * producer and create a new instance.\\n917:      * </p>\\n918:      * <p>\\n919:      * If the message format of the destination topic is not upgraded to 0.11.0.0, idempotent and transactional\\n920:      * produce requests will fail with an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedForMessageFormatException}\\n921:      * error. If this is encountered during a transaction, it is possible to abort and continue. But note that future\\n922:      * sends to the same topic will continue receiving the same exception until the topic is upgraded.\\n923:      * </p>\\n924:      * <p>\\n925:      * Note that callbacks will generally execute in the I/O thread of the producer and so should be reasonably fast or\\n926:      * they will delay the sending of messages from other threads. If you want to execute blocking or computationally\\n927:      * expensive callbacks it is recommended to use your own {@link java.util.concurrent.Executor} in the callback body\\n928:      * to parallelize processing.\\n929:      *\\n930:      * @param record The record to send\\n931:      * @param callback A user-supplied callback to execute when the record has been acknowledged by the server (null\\n932:      *        indicates no callback)\\n933:      *\\n934:      * @throws IllegalStateException if a transactional.id has been configured and no transaction has been started, or\\n935:      *                               when send is invoked after producer has been closed.\\n936:      * @throws InterruptException If the thread is interrupted while blocked\\n937:      * @throws SerializationException If the key or value are not valid objects given the configured serializers\\n938:      * @throws KafkaException If a Kafka related error occurs that does not belong to the public API exceptions.\\n939:      */\\n940:     @Override\\n941:     public Future<RecordMetadata> send(ProducerRecord<K, V> record, Callback callback) {\\n942:         // intercept the record, which can be potentially modified; this method does not throw exceptions\\n943:         ProducerRecord<K, V> interceptedRecord = this.interceptors.onSend(record);\\n944:         return doSend(interceptedRecord, callback);\\n945:     }\\n946: \\n947:     // Verify that this producer instance has not been closed. This method throws IllegalStateException if the producer\\n948:     // has already been closed.\\n949:     private void throwIfProducerClosed() {\\n950:         if (sender == null || !sender.isRunning())\\n951:             throw new IllegalStateException(\\\"Cannot perform operation after producer has been closed\\\");\\n952:     }\\n953: \\n954:     /**\\n955:      * Throws an exception if the transaction is in a prepared state.\\n956:      * In a two-phase commit (2PC) flow, once a transaction enters the prepared state,\\n957:      * only commit, abort, or complete operations are allowed.\\n958:      *\\n959:      * @throws IllegalStateException if any other operation is attempted in the prepared state.\\n960:      */\\n961:     private void If the producer is configured with acks = 0, the {@link RecordMetadata}\n845:      * will have offset = -1 because the producer does not wait for the acknowledgement from the broker.\n846:      * If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#CREATE_TIME CreateTime} is used by the topic, the timestamp\n847:      * will be the user provided timestamp or the record send time if the user did not specify a timestamp for the\n848:      * record. If {@link org.apache.kafka.common.record.TimestampType#LOG_APPEND_TIME LogAppendTime} is used for the\n849:      * topic, the timestamp will be the Kafka broker local time when the message is appended.\n850:      * <p>\n851:      * Since the send call is asynchronous it returns a {@link java.util.concurrent.Future Future} for the\n852:      * {@link RecordMetadata} that will be assigned to this record. Invoking {@link java.util.concurrent.Future#get()\n853:      * get()} on this future will block until the associated request completes and then return the metadata for the record\n854:      * or throw any exception that occurred while sending the record.\n855:      * <p>\n856:      * If you want to simulate a simple blocking call you can call the <code>get()</code> method immediately:\n857:      *\n858:      * <pre>\n859:      * {@code\n860:      * byte[] key = \"key\".getBytes();\n861:      * byte[] value = \"value\".getBytes();\n862:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\"my-topic\", key, value)\n863:      * producer.send(record).get();\n864:      * }</pre>\n865:      * <p>\n866:      * Fully non-blocking usage can make use of the {@link Callback} parameter to provide a callback that\n867:      * will be invoked when the request is complete.\n868:      *\n869:      * <pre>\n870:      * {@code\n871:      * ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]> record = new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(\"the-topic\", key, value);\n872:      * producer.send(myRecord,\n873:      *               new Callback() {\n874:      *                   public void onCompletion(RecordMetadata metadata, Exception e) {\n875:      *                       if(e != null) {\n876:      *                          e.printStackTrace();\n877:      *                       } else {\n878:      *                          System.out.println(\"The offset of the record we just sent is: \" + metadata.offset());\n879:      *                       }\n880:      *                   }\n881:      *               });\n882:      * }\n883:      * </pre>\n884:      *\n885:      * Callbacks for records being sent to the same partition are guaranteed to execute in order. That is, in the\n886:      * following example <code>callback1</code> is guaranteed to execute before <code>callback2</code>:\n887:      *\n888:      * <pre>\n889:      * {@code\n890:      * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key1, value1), callback1);\n891:      * producer.send(new ProducerRecord<byte[],byte[]>(topic, partition, key2, value2), callback2);\n892:      * }\n893:      * </pre>\n894:      * <p>\n895:      * When used as part of a transaction, it is not necessary to define a callback or check the result of the future\n896:      * in order to detect errors from <code>send</code>. If any of the send calls failed with an irrecoverable error,\n897:      * the final {@link #commitTransaction()} call will fail and throw the exception from the last failed send. When\n898:      * this happens, your application should call {@link #abortTransaction()} to reset the state and continue to send\n899:      * data.\n900:      * </p>\n901:      * <p>\n902:      * Some transactional send errors cannot be resolved with a call to {@link #abortTransaction()}.  In particular,\n903:      * if a transactional send finishes with a {@link ProducerFencedException}, a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.OutOfOrderSequenceException},\n904:      * a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException}, or an\n905:      * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.AuthorizationException}, then the only option left is to call {@link #close()}.\n906:      * Fatal errors cause the producer to enter a defunct state in which future API calls will continue to raise\n907:      * the same underlying error wrapped in a new {@link KafkaException}.\n908:      * </p>\n909:      * <p>\n910:      * It is a similar picture when idempotence is enabled, but no <code>transactional.id</code> has been configured.\n911:      * In this case, {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedVersionException} and\n912:      * {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.AuthorizationException} are considered fatal errors. However,\n913:      * {@link ProducerFencedException} does not need to be handled. Additionally, it is possible to continue\n914:      * sending after receiving an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.OutOfOrderSequenceException}, but doing so\n915:      * can result in out of order delivery of pending messages. To ensure proper ordering, you should close the\n916:      * producer and create a new instance.\n917:      * </p>\n918:      * <p>\n919:      * If the message format of the destination topic is not upgraded to 0.11.0.0, idempotent and transactional\n920:      * produce requests will fail with an {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.UnsupportedForMessageFormatException}\n921:      * error. If this is encountered during a transaction, it is possible to abort and continue. But note that future\n922:      * sends to the same topic will continue receiving the same exception until the topic is upgraded.\n923:      * </p>\n924:      * <p>\n925:      * Note that callbacks will generally execute in the I/O thread of the producer and so should be reasonably fast or\n926:      * they will delay the sending of messages from other threads. If you want to execute blocking or computationally\n927:      * expensive callbacks it is recommended to use your own {@link java.util.concurrent.Executor} in the callback body\n928:      * to parallelize processing.\n929:      *\n930:      * @param record The record to send\n931:      * @param callback A user-supplied callback to execute when the record has been acknowledged by the server (null\n932:      *        indicates no callback)\n933:      *\n934:      * @throws IllegalStateException if a transactional.id has been configured and no transaction has been started, or\n935:      *                               when send is invoked after producer has been closed.\n936:      * @throws InterruptException If the thread is interrupted while blocked\n937:      * @throws SerializationException If the key or value are not valid objects given the configured serializers\n938:      * @throws KafkaException If a Kafka related error occurs that does not belong to the public API exceptions.\n939:      */\n940:     @Override\n941:     public Future<RecordMetadata> send(ProducerRecord<K, V> record, Callback callback) {\n942:         // intercept the record, which can be potentially modified; this method does not throw exceptions\n943:         ProducerRecord<K, V> interceptedRecord = this.interceptors.onSend(record);\n944:         return doSend(interceptedRecord, callback);\n945:     }\n946: \n947:     // Verify that this producer instance has not been closed. **Purpose**: Convert network bytes back to typed objects for application code\n\n11. **ConsumerRecord Creation** (Consumer)\n    - **Location**: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/internals/CompletedFetch.java`\n    - `appendToLocalLog()` is called for each partition's records\n   - For each TopicIdPartition, retrieves the partition via `getPartitionOrException()` (line 1407)\n   - Calls `partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` (line 1408)\n\n### Leader Log Append\n**File: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/cluster/Partition.scala`**\n\n1. **Partition-Level Append** (line 1361):\n   - `Partition.appendRecordsToLeader()` checks if enough in-sync replicas (ISR) exist (line 1370)\n   - Throws `NotEnoughReplicasException` if min.isr not satisfied with acks=-1\n   - Calls `leaderLog.appendAsLeader()` on the UnifiedLog (line 1376)\n   - Increments high watermark if needed (line 1379)\n\n### UnifiedLog: Message Persistence\n**File: `storage/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/storage/internals/log/UnifiedLog.java`**\n\n1. **Append Implementation** (line 1024-1031):\n   - `UnifiedLog.appendAsLeader()` calls `append()` with validation flags\n   - `validateAndAssignOffsets=true` for CLIENT origin (line 1029)\n\n2. **Record Validation & Offset Assignment** (lines 1108-1152):\n   - If `validateAndAssignOffsets=true`:\n     - `LogValidator` validates each record and assigns monotonic offsets (line 1126)\n     - Validation includes: compression, timestamp range, batch format\n     - Offsets are assigned starting from `logEndOffset` (line 1110)\n   - Handles message format conversion if needed\n\n3. **Disk Write** (line 1224):\n   - `localLog.append(appendInfo.lastOffset(), validRecords)` writes to disk\n   - This writes RecordBatch format data to log segments\n   - Records are persisted in order by offset\n\n4. **Producer State Management** (lines 1227-1240):\n   - `ProducerStateManager.update()` tracks producer sequence numbers for idempotence (line 1228)\n   - Transaction index is updated for transactional writes (line 1234)\n   - `ProducerStateManager.updateMapEndOffset()` advances offset tracking (line 1240)\n\n5. **Flush to Disk** (line 1248):\n   - If `unflushedMessages >= flushInterval`, calls `flush(false)` to fsync to disk\n\n### Replication: Follower Fetch & Append\n**File: `core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/ReplicaFetcherThread.scala`**\n\n1. **Follower Fetches from Leader** (line 100-152):\n   - `ReplicaFetcherThread.processPartitionData()` receives fetched records from leader\n   - Converts fetched records to `MemoryRecords` (line 110)\n   - Validates offset continuity with log end offset (lines 112-114)\n\n2. **Follower Log Append** (line 121):\n   - Calls `partition.appendRecordsToFollowerOrFutureReplica()` (line 121)\n   - Appends records to follower's local log with same offsets as leader\n   - This ensures offset consistency across replicas\n\n3. **High Watermark Update** (lines 131-134):\n   - Updates follower's high watermark from leader's value (line 131)\n   - Completes delayed fetch requests once HW advances (line 156)\n\n### Summary: Broker Message Path\n```\nKafkaApis.handleProduceRequest()\n  ↓\nReplicaManager.handleProduceAppend() [ReplicaManager.scala:731]\n  ↓ (verify transactions if needed)\n  ↓ (call appendRecords)\nappendToLocalLog() [ReplicaManager.scala:1370]\n  ↓\nPartition.appendRecordsToLeader() [Partition.scala:1361]\n  ↓ (check ISR)\nUnifiedLog.appendAsLeader() [UnifiedLog.java:1024]\n  ↓ (validate & assign offsets)\nLogValidator.validateMessagesAndAssignOffsets() [UnifiedLog.java:1126]\n  ↓ (write to disk)\nLocalLog.append() [UnifiedLog.java:1224]\n  ↓ (update state)\nProducerStateManager.update() [UnifiedLog.java:1228]\n  ↓ (flush if needed)\nflush() [UnifiedLog.java:1248]\n\nREPLICATION:\nReplicaFetcherThread.processPartitionData() [ReplicaFetcherThread.scala:101]\n  ↓\nPartition.appendRecordsToFollowerOrFutureReplica() [ReplicaFetcherThread.scala:121]\n  ↓\nUnifiedLog.appendAsFollower() [similar to leader append]\n  ↓\nHigh watermark update [ReplicaFetcherThread.scala:131]\n```\n\n---\n\n## Q3: Consumer-Side Fetch and Delivery\n\n### Consumer Poll Entry Point\n**File: `clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/KafkaConsumer.java`**\n\n1. **Poll API** (line 894-895):\n   -
